**Example**:

Iteration 4: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **New Instruction:**

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and data analysis based on a given set of constraints. The task involves two sub-problems:

1. **Overall Probability of Promotion**:  
   Given a media company with 100 journalists (60 women, 40 men), and the probability of promotion based on gender and experience, calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist is promoted to a leadership position. You are provided with the following conditional probabilities:  
   - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
   - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
   - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
   - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

   Additionally, you are given the following probabilities:  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced ($ P(E | F) = 0.7 $)  
   - 60% of male journalists are experienced ($ P(E | M) = 0.6 $)  

   You must apply the **law of total probability** to compute the overall probability $ P(L) $, and ensure that all probabilities are correctly calculated and presented.

2. **Minimum Increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ for Gender Representation**:  
   The company aims to increase the representation of women in leadership roles to at least 50%. Assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant, determine the **minimum increase** in $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve this goal. You must provide a clear explanation of how the increase is calculated and ensure that the final result meets the requirement of at least 24 words with all capital letters in the response.

**Additional Constraints:**
- **All capital letters** must appear at least 24 times in the response.  
- Use **markdown** to highlight key sections of the solution.  
- The response must be structured in a clear, logical format with proper explanations for each step.  
- Ensure that the response satisfies all constraints and provides a complete, accurate solution to the task.

Iteration 6: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions

You are to perform a task involving probability and conditional reasoning, specifically in the context of a media company's promotion system. The task involves calculating the overall probability of a journalist being promoted to a leadership position based on their gender and experience level, and then determining the minimum increase in a specific conditional probability required to meet a company's goal of increasing the representation of women in leadership roles.

### Input Format

- The company has 100 journalists: 60 women and 40 men.
- 70% of female journalists are experienced, and 60% of male journalists are experienced.
- Historical data provides the following conditional probabilities:
  1. $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $
  2. $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $
  3. $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $
  4. $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $

### Task Description

1. **Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist is promoted to a leadership position.**
   - Use the law of total probability to compute the total probability of promotion across all gender and experience groups.

2. **Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve a 50% representation of women in leadership roles.**
   - Assume the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.
   - The goal is to increase the proportion of women in leadership roles to at least 50%.

### Constraints

- **Punctuation:** Avoid the use of periods (i.e., dots) as punctuation.
- **Capital Letters:** Words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.
- **Word Count:** The response should be less than 833 words.
- **Clarity:** The response must be clear, concise, and logically structured, with proper mathematical notation and explanations.

### Output Format

- A detailed explanation of the calculations and reasoning for both sub-problems.
- A final answer to the second sub-problem, specifying the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve the 50% goal.

### Example Output Structure

```
### Sub-Problem 1: Overall Probability of Promotion

We are given:

- Total journalists: 100  
- Female journalists: 60  
- Male journalists: 40  
- Experiential distribution:  
  - 70% of female journalists are experienced → 42 female experienced  
  - 60% of male journalists are experienced → 24 male experienced  
- Non-experienced journalists:  
  - 30% of female journalists → 18 female non-experienced  
  - 40% of male journalists → 16 male non-experienced  

We are to calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist is promoted to a leadership position, using the given conditional probabilities:

1. $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
2. $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
3. $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
4. $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $

---

### Step 1: Calculate the number of journalists in each category

- Female experienced: 42  
- Female non-experienced: 18  
- Male experienced: 24  
- Male non-experienced: 16  

---

### Step 2: Calculate the probability of promotion for each group

- **Female experienced:**  
  $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
  Contribution: $ 42 \times 0.3 = 12.6 $

- **Female non-experienced:**  
  $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
  Contribution: $ 18 \times 0.1 = 1.8 $

- **Male experienced:**  
  $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
  Contribution: $ 24 \times 0.25 = 6 $

- **Male non-experienced:**  
  $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  
  Contribution: $ 16 \times 0.05 = 0.8 $

---

### Step 3: Total number of promoted journalists

Total promoted = $ 12.6 + 1.8 + 6 + 0.8 = 21.2 $

---

### Step 4: Overall probability of promotion

$$
P(L) = \frac{21.2}{100} = 0.212 \text{ or } 21.2\%
$$

---

### Sub-Problem 2: Minimum Increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ to Achieve 50% Women in Leadership

To achieve a 50% representation of women in leadership roles, we need at least 50 out of 100 leadership positions to be held by women.

Let’s denote the new probability of promotion for female non-experienced journalists as $ P(L | F, N') $. We need to find the minimum value of $ P(L | F, N') $ such that the number of women promoted is at least 50.

Let’s assume the current number of women promoted is 12.6 (from female experienced) + 1.8 (from female non-experienced) = 14.4.

To reach 50 women in leadership, we need an additional 35.6 promotions from women.

Let’s denote the number of female non-experienced journalists as 18 (from earlier calculation). To achieve 35.6 promotions from women, we need:

$$
P(L | F, N') \times 18 \geq 35.6
$$

$$
P(L | F, N') \geq \frac{35.6}{18} \approx 1.978
$$

However, probabilities cannot exceed 1. Therefore, the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ is **0.978** (i.e., from 0.1 to 1.078), which is not possible. Hence, the minimum achievable probability is **0.1** (no increase), and the goal cannot be met with the current setup.

Thus, the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve 50% women in leadership is **0.0** (no increase), but this is not feasible. Therefore, it is not possible to achieve 50% women in leadership roles with the current setup.
```

```
- A company with 100 journalists, of which 60 are women and 40 are men.
- Historical data on the probability of promotion based on gender and experience:
  - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $
  - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $
  - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $
  - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $
- Additional information:
  - 70% of female journalists are experienced.
  - 60% of male journalists are experienced.

You are to:
1. Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist is promoted to a leadership position.
2. Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% female representation in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and not experienced journalists remains constant.

### Constraints

- Use only mathematical reasoning and conditional probability.
- Provide answers in a clear, structured format with proper explanation.

You are to perform a task involving conditional probability calculations and data analysis for a media company's promotion process. The task includes:

1. **Data Input**:  
   - A media company has 100 journalists, with 60 women and 40 men.  
   - 70% of women are experienced, and 60% of men are experienced.  
   - Conditional probabilities for promotion are given:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $

2. **Sub-problems to Solve**:  
   - **Sub-Problem 1**: Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist is promoted, regardless of gender or experience.  
   - **Sub-Problem 2**: Determine the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% female leadership representation, assuming the distribution of experienced and not experienced journalists remains constant.  

3. **Constraints**:  
   - Your response must be structured in **two paragraphs**, separated by **two line breaks**.  
   - The response must contain **less than 36 sentences**.  
   - All lowercase words must appear **at most 3 times**.  
   - Include a **palindrome** in your response.  
   - Words with **all capital letters** must appear **at least 24 times**.  

4. **Output Requirements**:  
   - Provide a **complete, well-structured analysis** of both sub-problems.  
   - Ensure the solution is **clear, logical, and mathematically sound**.  
   - Use **proper formatting** (e.g., equations, calculations, and explanations).  

5. **Additional Notes**:  
   - Use **clear headings** for each sub-problem (e.g., "Sub-Problem 1: Overall Probability of Promotion").  
   - Include a **palindrome** in your final response (e.g., "abba" or "racecar").
```

```
Iteration 25: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions

You are to solve a mathematical or logical problem involving probability and conditional expectations, based on a given set of data and constraints. The task involves calculating an overall probability of a specific event (promotion to leadership) based on gender and experience levels. The problem includes sub-problems that require applying the law of total probability and conditional probabilities.

### Task Description

Given a media company with 100 journalists, where 60 are women and 40 are men, and the following conditional probabilities for promotion to leadership:

- $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $
- $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $
- $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $
- $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $

You are also given that:
- 70% of female journalists are experienced ($ P(E | F) = 0.7 $)
- 60% of male journalists are experienced ($ P(E | M) = 0.6 $)
```

Iteration 33: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions

You are to perform a task that involves solving a complex probability problem related to a media company's promotion process. The task includes the following components:

### 1. **Understanding the Problem**
   - You are given a scenario involving a media company with 100 journalists, 60 of whom are women and 40 are men.
   - The company has historical data on the probability of a journalist being promoted to a leadership position, given their gender and experience level.
   - The probabilities are:
     1. $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $
     2. $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $
     3. $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $
     4. $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $

### 2. **Analyzing the Data**
   - You are to calculate the **overall probability** that a randomly selected journalist is promoted to a leadership position, regardless of gender or experience.
   - You are also to determine the **minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $** required to achieve a leadership promotion rate of at least 50%, assuming the distribution of experienced and not experienced journalists remains constant.

### 3. **Formatting the Response**
   - Provide your solution in a structured format with clear sections.
   - Use markdown to highlight key calculations and results.
   - Ensure all mathematical expressions are properly formatted using LaTeX.
   - Include a brief explanation of your approach and the assumptions made during the calculation.
   - End your response with the word "END" to indicate completion.

### 4. **Constraints**
   - All calculations must be based on the given data and probabilities.
   - The solution must be presented in a logical, step-by-step manner.
   - Ensure that the final answer is accurate and clear.
   - If the problem requires an increase in $ P(L | F, N) $, provide the exact value and the reasoning behind it.

### 5. **Additional Requirements**
   - Include a brief explanation of how the promotion probability is calculated for each gender and experience level.
   - Use appropriate terminology and avoid any markdown formatting unless explicitly required.
   - Ensure the response is well-organized and easy to follow.
   - If the problem is unsolvable with the given data, clearly state that the problem is unsolvable under the current constraints.

### 6. **Output Format**
   - Use clear headings and subheadings to organize the solution.
   - Use bold text for key terms (e.g., "Overall Probability", "Minimum Increase").
   - Include all necessary calculations and intermediate steps.
   - Present the final answer in a boxed format as requested.

### 7. **Final Check**
   - Verify that all calculations are correct and that the final answer meets the problem's requirements.
   - Ensure that the response is concise, accurate, and well-structured.

---

### **Example Output (Template)**

**Sub-Problem 1: Overall Probability of Promotion**

- Total journalists: 100  
- Female journalists: 60  
- Male journalists: 40  
- Experienced journalists: 70% of female journalists = 42  
- Not experienced journalists: 30% of female journalists = 18  
- Experienced journalists: 60% of male journalists = 24  
- Not experienced journalists: 40% of male journalists = 16  

- Female experienced: $ 42 \times 0.3 = 12.6 $  
- Female not experienced: $ 18 \times 0.1 = 1.8 $  
- Male experienced: $ 24 \times 0.25 = 6 $  
- Male not experienced: $ 16 \times 0.05 = 0.8 $  

- Total promoted: $ 12.6 + 1.8 + 6 + 0.8 = 21.2 $  
- Total journalists: $ 42 + 18 + 24 + 16 = 100 $  
- Overall probability: $ \frac{21.2}{100} = 0.212 $ or 21.2%

---

### **Final Answer**
$$
\boxed{0.212}
$$

**Minimum Increase in $ P(L | F, N) $:**
- To achieve at least 50% promotion rate, we need $ \frac{50}{100} = 0.5 $.
- Currently, $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $.
- The required increase is $ 0.5 - 0.1 = 0.4 $.

Thus, the minimum increase required is **0.4**.

---

### **END**

### Input Format  
The input consists of a series of tasks involving probability, data analysis, and logical reasoning. Each task includes:  
1. **Scenario Description**: A problem involving probabilities, data distributions, or logical deductions.  
2. **Probability Rules**: A set of conditional probabilities (e.g., $ P(L | F, E) $, $ P(L | M, N) $, etc.).  
3. **Data Values**: Numerical values such as total number of journalists, gender distribution, experience percentages, and conditional probabilities.  

### Task Requirements  
1. **Calculate Overall Probability**:  
   - Determine the overall probability of a journalist being promoted to a leadership position, considering gender and experience.  
   - Use the given conditional probabilities and data to compute the expected number of promotions per group (e.g., female experienced, female not experienced, male experienced, male not experienced).  
   - Sum the expected promotions across all groups to find the total probability.  

2. **Determine Minimum Probability Increase**:  
   - Given a target gender representation (e.g., at least 50% women in leadership roles), calculate the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve this goal.  
   - Assume the distribution of experienced and not experienced journalists remains constant.  
   - Ensure that the response includes at least 24 words with all capital letters.  

3. **Conditional Probability Analysis**:  
   - Use the provided conditional probabilities to determine the probability of promotion for each gender and experience group.  
   - Apply the law of total probability to compute the overall probability of promotion.  

4. **Punctuation and Formatting Constraints**:  
   - Avoid the use of periods (.) as punctuation.  
   - Ensure that words with all capital letters appear less than 9 times in the response.  
   - Limit the total word count to less than 833 words.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information  
- **Probability Modeling**: The problem involves conditional probability and the law of total probability.  
- **Data Analysis**: The task requires grouping data by gender and experience, then computing expected outcomes based on given probabilities.  
- **Logistical Constraints**: The problem includes a fixed total number of journalists (100), with specific gender and experience distributions.  
- **Targeted Output**: The response must include a clear calculation of the overall probability, a logical explanation of the steps, and a final answer that satisfies all constraints.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
- **Step-by-Step Calculation**: Break the problem into smaller parts (e.g., group calculations, conditional probability applications).  
- **Use of Conditional Probability**: Apply the law of total probability to combine probabilities across different groups.  
- **Data Grouping**: Organize data by gender and experience to compute expected outcomes.  
- **Constraint Compliance**: Ensure that all formatting, punctuation, and word-count constraints are strictly followed.  

### Final Instructions  
Provide a complete, well-structured response that:  
1. Calculates the overall probability of promotion using the given data and conditional probabilities.  
2. Determines the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve the target gender representation.  
3. Applies the law of total probability and ensures all constraints (punctuation, word count, capital letters) are met.  
4. Includes at least 24 words with all capital letters and adheres to the specified formatting and word limits.
